## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (rate laws / integrated rate equations)
**Analysis**: The target dA_dt is explicitly the time-derivative of a reactant concentration A, which is the standard setup for ordinary-differential-equation (ODE) rate laws in chemical kinetics. With only (t, A) available, the most likely governing forms are autonomous rate laws dA_dt = f(A) and their time-dependent extensions (e.g., driven, inhibited, or catalyst-deactivating kinetics).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order rate law: dA_dt = -c0 (constant-rate consumption, e.g., surface-limited or saturated kinetics)
- First-order rate law: dA_dt = -c0 * A (unimolecular decay, dilute limit)
- Second-order (self-reaction) rate law: dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (bimolecular 2A → products)
- General n-th order (power-law) rate law: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (empirical or mechanistic effective order)
- Autocatalytic (quadratic growth/decay) form: dA_dt = c0 * A - c1 * A**2 (logistic-like kinetics from autocatalysis plus depletion/termination)
- Reversible first-order relaxation (linear to equilibrium): dA_dt = -c0 * (A - c1) (approach to equilibrium concentration c1)
- Cubic/quintic normal-form kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A - c1 * A**3 (bistability/criticality approximations in kinetic models)
- Rational inhibition / crowding: dA_dt = -c0 * A / (c1 + A) (rate suppressed at high A by self-inhibition/transport limits)
- Rational with higher-order inhibition: dA_dt = -c0 * A / (c1 + A**c2) (generalized inhibition/limited accessibility)
- Saturating production minus decay: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) - c2 * A (net balance of saturable formation and linear loss)
- Time-driven forcing (periodic feed/drive): dA_dt = -c0 * A + c1 * sin(c2 * t) (externally modulated input/removal)
- Time-dependent rate coefficient (deactivation/aging): dA_dt = -(c0 + c1 * t) * A (effective rate increases/decreases linearly with time)
- Exponential-in-time rate coefficient (activation/deactivation): dA_dt = -c0 * exp(c1 * t) * A (catalyst activation/deactivation or changing conditions)
- Finite-time quench/turn-on (smooth switching): dA_dt = -c0 * (0.5 + 0.5 * tanh(c1 * (t - c2))) * A (reaction turns on/off around time c2)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Mass-action consumption of a single species → polynomial in A (e.g., A, A**2, A**n) with negative sign for depletion
- Approach to equilibrium or steady state → linear relaxation in (A - c) giving exponential-in-time A(t) when integrated
- Autocatalysis / self-amplification → positive linear term in A paired with negative higher-order term (A**2 or A**3) to prevent blow-up
- Self-inhibition / transport limitation at high concentration → rational forms with A in numerator and (c + A**n) in denominator
- Bistability / switching kinetics (effective reduced models) → odd-polynomial normal forms like c*A - c*A**3
- Changing experimental conditions (mixing, feed, catalyst deactivation) → explicit time dependence multiplying A, e.g., (c0 + c1*t)*A or exp(c*t)*A
- External periodic drive (pH cycling, illumination, pulsed feed) → additive sinusoidal term in t in dA_dt
- Non-negativity of concentration → structures that yield dA_dt → 0 as A → 0 (e.g., proportional-to-A forms) to avoid unphysical negative A
- Stiff kinetics / rapid initial transients → higher powers of A or strong nonlinear rational inhibition producing sharp early-time slopes
- Competing pathways lumping → sums of multiple A-powers (e.g., -c0*A - c1*A**2) indicating parallel first- and second-order loss

GT Equivalence Verification (CRK0)
============================================================
GT: -c0*A**c1 + c2*_z*A**c3/(c4*A**c5 + c6)
Candidate formulas: 56

GT is the fixed function (independent of `t`):
\[
f(A)= -0.18997742423620262\,A^2 \;+\; \frac{0.45987487478174419\,A^2}{0.7497988950401423\,A^4+1}.
\]
So it is a **purely algebraic rational function** of \(A\) (polynomial + rational term), with **only even powers** and no `Abs`, `log`, `exp`, `sin`, `tanh`, etc. Any candidate containing transcendental pieces must set their coefficients to 0 (or otherwise collapse them) to match for all \(A\). Also any candidate depending on `t` must eliminate that dependence.

Below, for each candidate, I check whether it can be reduced (by choosing constants) to exactly \(-kA^2 + mA^2/(nA^4+1)\) with the specific fixed numeric coefficients.

---

### 1
Has `exp(A*c1)` and `exp(c4*sin(...))` terms over `(A*c2+1)`. To match a rational function for all \(A\), all exponential/sine-dependent numerators must vanish ⇒ set coefficients of those terms to 0. Then expression becomes `c7/(A*c2+1)` which is of form constant/(linear). GT is not constant/(linear). No match.

### 2
Linear + constants + `log(Abs(A))` and `log(exp(A))` structure. Logs cannot equal a rational function for all \(A\) unless their coefficients are 0. Setting log coefficients 0 leaves `A*c0 + c1`, not GT. No match.

### 3
Has `log(...)`. Kill log term ⇒ polynomial `A*c0 + c2*A**c1 + c3`. Can choose `c1=2` to get quadratic, but then it’s just a polynomial, cannot produce the rational \(A^2/(A^4+1)\) term. No match.

### 4
Quadratic + linear + log. Kill log ⇒ polynomial with linear term(s). GT has no linear term and has rational part. No match.

### 5
Quadratic + linear + log. Same issue. No match.

### 6
Cubic + linear + log. Cannot become GT. No match.

### 7
Linear + sin + log. Must kill sin/log ⇒ linear+constant only. No match.

### 8
Uses `Abs(A)` and denominator `c1+Abs(A)**5`. Even if you try to mimic \(A^4\) in denominator, power is fixed at 5 and absolute value introduces non-analytic kink at 0; GT is smooth polynomial/rational. No match.

### 9
Rational with denominator `A**5 + c1`. GT denominator is quartic in \(A\) (specifically \(0.7498 A^4+1\)) and overall structure is polynomial + \(A^2/(A^4+1)\). With `A**5` you cannot match for all \(A\). No match.

### 10
Contains `A*c1/(A+c2)` and log. Kill log ⇒ `A*c0 + A*c1/(A+c2) + c3`. That rational term has linear denominator; cannot equal \(A^2/(A^4+1)\) for all \(A\). No match.

### 11
Same as 10 but log depends on `t` too. Must kill log anyway; remaining still wrong rational form. No match.

### 12
Denominator `A**3*c1+1` and has `exp(A*c3)`. Kill exp terms ⇒ rational with denominator cubic in \(A\), not quartic. No match.

### 13
Has `t` inside log. Must kill log term ⇒ polynomial `A*c0 + c2*A**c1 + c3`. Cannot create GT rational part. No match.

### 14
Logs present (including `log(A**3*c6+c7)`). Kill logs ⇒ linear+constant only. No match.

### 15
Similar: logs; killing them leaves linear+constant. No match.

### 16
Has \(A^{1/3}\log(Ac1+1)\) and sin. Kill those ⇒ `A*c2 + c3`, not GT. No match.

### 17
Sum of exponentials and log. To become rational, must kill all transcendental terms ⇒ becomes 0. Not GT. No match.

### 18
Has `Abs(A**3)` in denominator `c1*Abs(A**3)+1` and logs. Even killing logs, you get rational in \(|A|^3\), not \(A^4\), and absolute value mismatch. No match.

### 19
Has `A*c0/(A+c1)` plus exponentials. Kill exponentials ⇒ `A*c0/(A+c1)` only, wrong form. No match.

### 20
Denominator `A**4 + c1` (promising), but also includes `log(...)` terms. Kill log terms ⇒
\[
\frac{A^5 c0 + A^4 c2 + A c6 + A c7 + c8}{A^4+c1}.
\]
This is a rational function with denominator \(A^4+c1\), but GT is **polynomial +** \(\frac{A^2}{0.7498A^4+1}\). You could rewrite GT over common denominator \(0.7498A^4+1\):
\[
f(A)=\frac{-0.1899774A^2(0.7497989A^4+1)+0.4598749A^2}{0.7497989A^4+1}
=\frac{-0.14245A^6+0.269897A^2}{0.7497989A^4+1}.
\]
So GT as a single fraction has numerator with **only \(A^6\) and \(A^2\)** terms, no \(A^5,A^4,A^1,A^0\).
Candidate 20 numerator basis (after killing logs) allows \(A^5, A^4, A^1, A^0\) but **not \(A^6\) or \(A^2\)**. Multiplying out: \(A^5/(A^4+c1)\) behaves like \(A\) at infinity, not \(A^2\). There is no way to produce an \(A^6\) numerator term. No match.

### 21
Has logs and a sine of a log. Must kill transcendental parts ⇒ linear+constant only. No match.

Denominator `A**5 + c1` and sine. Wrong power and transcendental. No match.

### 29
Denominator `A**4 + c1` and purely algebraic rational (good class), but terms are:
\[
\frac{A^6 c0 + A^5 c2 + A^4(c3+c4) + A^2 c5 + A c6 + c7}{A^4+c1}.
\]
We need GT as single fraction with denominator proportional to \(A^4\) plus constant. Set \(c1=1/0.7497988950401423\) and multiply numerator accordingly? Actually candidate denominator is \(A^4+c1\); GT denominator is \(0.7498A^4+1\). These are proportional if we choose \(c1 = 1/0.7498\) and then scale numerator by \(0.7498\). That part is feasible.
But GT numerator (in the single-fraction form) has only \(A^6\) and \(A^2\) terms. Candidate 29 can match that by setting:
- \(c2=0\) (kill \(A^5\))
- \(c3+c4=0\) (kill \(A^4\))
- \(c6=0\) (kill \(A\))
- \(c7=0\) (kill constant)
and keep \(c0\) and \(c5\) to match \(A^6\) and \(A^2\) coefficients.
So structurally candidate 29 **can** represent \(\frac{\alpha A^6 + \beta A^2}{A^4+\gamma}\), which matches GT’s single-fraction form.

Now check if coefficients can be matched exactly:
GT single-fraction form:
\[
\frac{-0.1899774A^2(0.7497989A^4+1)+0.4598749A^2}{0.7497989A^4+1}
=\frac{(-0.1899774\cdot 0.7497989)A^6 + (-0.1899774+0.4598749)A^2}{0.7497989A^4+1}.
\]
So numerator coefficients are:
- \(A^6\): \(-0.18997742423620262 \times 0.7497988950401423\) (some negative value)
- \(A^2\): \(0.26989745054554157\) (since 0.45987487478174419 − 0.18997742423620262)

Candidate 29 after choosing denominator proportionality:
Let denominator be \(A^4+c1\). To equal GT denominator \(0.7498A^4+1\), we need a constant factor \(k\) such that
\(A^4+c1 = k(0.7498A^4+1)\).
Matching coefficients gives \(1 = k\cdot 0.7498\Rightarrow k=1/0.7498\), and \(c1 = k\cdot 1 = 1/0.7498\). Good.
Then candidate value is
\[
\frac{A^6 c0 + A^2 c5}{A^4+c1}
=\frac{A^6 c0 + A^2 c5}{(1/0.7498)(0.7498A^4+1)}
=0.7498\cdot \frac{A^6 c0 + A^2 c5}{0.7498A^4+1}.
\]
So we need
\[
0.7498\,c0 = -0.1899774\cdot 0.7498 \Rightarrow c0=-0.1899774,
\]
\[
0.7498\,c5 = 0.2698974505 \Rightarrow c5 = 0.2698974505/0.7498.
\]
Both are valid real choices. Therefore candidate 29 **can be made exactly equal** to GT.

GT: -c0*A**c1 + c2*_z*A**c3/(c4*A**c5 + c6)
Candidates evaluated: 56
Matched candidate IDs: [29, 30]
Matched candidates: ["A**6*c0/(A**4 + c1) + A**5*c2/(A**4 + c1) + A**4*c3/(A**4 + c1) + A**4*c4/(A**4 + c1) + A**2*c5/(A**4 + c1) + A*c6/(A**4 + c1) + c7/(A**4 + c1)", "A**2*A**c0*c1/(A**c0 + c2) + A**2*c3/(A**c0 + c2) + A*A**c0*c4/(A**c0 + c2) + A*c5/(A**c0 + c2) + A**c0*c6/(A**c0 + c2) + A**c0*c7/(A**c0 + c2) + c8/(A**c0 + c2)"]

I need to analyze each candidate against the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT:** `-0.18997742423620262*A**2 + 0.45987487478174419*A**2/(0.7497988950401423*A**4 + 1)`

Let me simplify: GT = `-c0*A^2 + c0*_z*A^2/(c4*A^4 + 1)` where the rational term is `0.4599*A^2/(0.7498*A^4 + 1)`.

The GT is a sum of two terms:
1. A polynomial term: `-0.19*A^2`
2. A rational term: `0.46*A^2/(0.75*A^4 + 1)`

Combined over common denominator: `[-0.19*A^2*(0.75*A^4+1) + 0.46*A^2] / (0.75*A^4+1)`
= `[-0.1425*A^6 - 0.19*A^2 + 0.46*A^2] / (0.75*A^4+1)`
= `[-0.1425*A^6 + 0.27*A^2] / (0.75*A^4+1)`

So GT = `(c_a*A^6 + c_b*A^2) / (c_c*A^4 + 1)` — a rational function with numerator having A^6 and A^2 terms, denominator having A^4 and constant terms.

Key structural features of GT:
- It's a function of A only (no t dependence)
- It's a rational function equivalent to `(αA^6 + βA^2)/(γA^4 + 1)`
- No exponentials, no logarithms, no trigonometric functions, no absolute values needed (A ≥ 0)

Let me check each candidate systematically. For candidates with exp, log, sin, etc., these basis functions cannot be eliminated unless their coefficients are zero, which would typically destroy the rational structure needed.

**Candidates with exponentials/logs/sin that cannot reduce to a pure rational function:**

For any candidate containing `exp(A*c)`, `log(...)`, `sin(...)`, `tanh(...)` terms that are essential (can't be zeroed without losing all structure), these cannot match.

Let me identify candidates that could potentially be pure rational functions in A:

**Candidate 9:** `(A^7*c0 + A^6*c2 + A^5*c3 + A^2*c4 + A*c5 + A*c6 + c7)/(A^5 + c1)`

GT = `(αA^6 + βA^2)/(γA^4 + 1)`. This has denominator A^5 + c1, not A^4 + c1. The degrees don't match. Setting c0=0 gives `(A^6*c2 + A^5*c3 + A^2*c4 + A*(c5+c6) + c7)/(A^5+c1)`. For this to equal `(αA^6+βA^2)/(γA^4+1)`, we'd need cross-multiplication to work: `(c2*A^6+c3*A^5+c4*A^2+(c5+c6)*A+c7)(γA^4+1) = (αA^6+βA^2)(A^5+c1)`. The right side has A^11 and A^6 as highest terms. The left has A^10 as highest. This can't work unless γ=0, but then denominator is constant. Let me try: if γ=0, GT = αA^6+βA^2, and candidate = polynomial after division. With c3=0, c5+c6=0, c7=0: `(c2*A^6+c4*A^2)/(A^5+c1)` — this doesn't simplify to a polynomial. No match.

**Candidate 29:** `(A^6*c0 + A^5*c2 + A^4*(c3+c4) + A^2*c5 + A*c6 + c7)/(A^4 + c1)`

This has denominator `A^4 + c1` — matching! Set c2=0, c6=0, c7=0, c3+c4 = any value. We get `(c0*A^6 + (c3+c4)*A^4 + c5*A^2)/(A^4+c1)`. 

Cross-multiply with GT: `(αA^6+βA^2)/(γA^4+1)`. Set c1 = 1/γ, then multiply: need `(c0*A^6+(c3+c4)*A^4+c5*A^2)*γ = (αA^6+βA^2)`. So c0*γ=α, (c3+c4)*γ=0 → c3+c4=0, c5*γ=β. This works! **MATCH!**

**Candidate 30:** With c0=4, this becomes `(A^6*c1+A^2*c3+...)/(A^4+c2)` structure. Setting appropriate constants to zero, this could work. Let me check: c0=4, denominator = A^4+c2. Numerator terms: A^2*A^4*c1 + A^2*c3 + A*A^4*c4 + A*c5 + A^4*(c6+c7) + c8 = A^6*c1+A^5*c4+A^4*(c6+c7)+A^2*c3+A*c5+c8. Set c4=c5=c6+c7=c8=0. Get (A^6*c1+A^2*c3)/(A^4+c2). **MATCH!**
